RATING: 8
I like it better than Marvel Legendary, which I like quite a bit, because it's a better pure coop.  It's more difficult (though not by a lot from my limited experience), there are no points to earn and no single winner.  The Coordinate keyword adds far more cooperation to the game and takes away the feeling of being multiplayer solitaire (which I normally like, but is not a good thing for a coop), and I think makes it scale better with more players since you have more opportunities to play Coordinate cards.  My only complaint is that some of the images are a bit too gory for my taste.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
So this is an outstanding thematic experience if you want to play through the Alien movies. But it's a terrible deckbuilder.

Why? Well, the primary reason is that it uses a Star Realms style trade row -- instead of piles of specific cards a la Dominion, there are always 5 cards visible to buy, dealt randomly from a huge deck. This works fine in Star Realms and other deckbuilders, sure, but the problem here is that you're playing a cooperative game against a constructed deck that gets harder at a fast pace. So if good cards for your build don't come out, or the entire trade row is too expensive for anyone to buy anything for several turns, etc., you can easily get totally screwed by that alone. This problem is exacerbated with more players since it gets harder and harder to make every deck "good". 

There are other minor problems, like the way the card combos work -- every card has two symbols for possible combos, but if you mix and match characters instead of just playing the 4 preset movies over and over, half of those combo icons basically become useless. But really that main problem is the one outlined in the paragraph above: a curated and aggressively timed Hive deck is too hard of a match for a few bumbling space marines grabbing random tools out of a box.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
1st play: I quite enjoyed this.  A refinement of the Legendary system, I like the exploration of the card rows and the sense of danger from flipping over the cards to see what happens.  The coordinate mechanism is cool, and allows for some interactivity.  It's not too difficult a choice, but it's nice to feel like you're able to contribute.  The theme is less awesome for me than Marvel, but the game is better.

2nd play: Quite a bit harder this game, and I ended up dying almost without any ability to react or prevent it.  I don't like when games make you lose without an ability to react.  In this case, I could probably have taken different actions to prevent it, but to do so would have been pretty sub-optimal (waste 3 attack points out of fear of a chestburster), and I took a strike that dumped my hand without any way to prevent or avoid it.  I still like the game, but not as much as the first play.

RATING: 5
My initial reaction was very negative. After playing the full campaign and playing each scenario multiple times I think I have a more clear view. My honest feeling about the game are "Meh". Its okay. There are no real meaningful choices, for a deckbuilder there isn't that many options to thin your deck, the game sometimes feels like it just chuggs along. On the other hand, those totally random moments that make no sense but are just epic are really exciting. That one in a hundred chance when you actually get a good hand and you get to do a lot of things to almost turn the game around, and then even with all your planning you die/lose because of a cheep card reveal wile frustrating is still exciting. I could take it or leave it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Αξιόλογο deck building game βασισμένο πάνω στην τετραλογία των ταινιών Alien. Μου άρεσε αρκετά η εικονογραφηση που σε βάζει στο κλίμα του παιχνιδιού. :) Οι κανόνες είναι σχετικά απλοί. Αρχικά διαλέγουμε ποια objectives θα παίξουμε. Ουσιαστικά ποιά ταινία θέλουμε να παίξουμε αν και υπάρχει η δυνατότητα να μπερδέψουμε τα objectives. Αυτά καθορίζουν ποιες κάρτες/εχθρούς θα αντιμετωπίσουμε αλλά και το ποιες κάρτες θα είναι διαθέσιμες για αγορά από τους παίκτες. 

Όλοι ξεκινάμε με ένα σχεδόν πανομοιότυπο deck και το βελτιώνουμε στην πορεία. Οι εχθροί βγαίνουν σιγά σιγά και προσπαθούν να φτάσουν σε μας. Μπορούμε να σκανάρουμε τις θέσεις τους και να τους επιτεθούμε όσο ακόμα είναι μακριά, αλλιώς τους αφήνουμε να έρθουν πάνω μας και ότι γίνει. :p 

Η συνεργασία μεταξύ των παικτών γίνεται μέσω του Coordinate μηχανισμού. Είναι ουσιαστικά κάποιες κάρτες που σου επιτρέπουν να δώσεις δώρο ένα σύμβολο στο συμπαίκτη σου επιτρέποντας τον έτσι να χρησιμοποιήσει το μπόνους ability κάποιων καρτών. Απλός μηχανισμός και δουλεύει ικανοποιητικά. :meeple:

Να προσθέσω πως υπάρχουν και variant rules για τους νεκρούς παίκτες να επιστρέφουν σαν Alien στο παιχνίδι, ή να υπάρχει traitor ανάμεσα στους παίκτες αλλά δεν δοκιμάσαμε κάτι από αυτά. Ακούγεται ενδιαφέρον πάντως. Επίσης μπορείς να ενώσεις το παιχνίδι με οποιδήποτε άλλο της εταιρίας και να έχεις πχ Alien μαζί με υπερήρωες της Marvel αλλά δεν μπορώ να φανταστώ γιατί να κάνει κάποιος κάτι τέτοιο. :shake:

Στα αρνητικά να βάλω την ύπαρξη player elimination αφού κάλιστα μπορεί κάποιος παίχτης να πεθάνει αλλά οι υπόλοιποι συνεχίζουν τον αγώνα. Είναι θεματικό μεν, αλλά δεν είναι γενικά ωραίο κάποιος από την παρέα να μην παίζει. Αυτό λύνεται με το Variant που αναφέρω παραπάνω ενώ αρνητικό είναι και το μπόλικο στήστιμο/μάζεμα του παιχνιδιού καθώς όλες οι κάρτες πρέπει να ξεχωριστούν. Κλασικό πρόβλημα σε πολλά deck building games. :(

Παίζεται ευχάριστα, ειδικά αν είσαι φαν των ταινιών και αναγνωρίζεις πρόσωπα και καταστάσεις.

RATING: 9.3
Seems like a jumbled mess when you first open the box, but then as you organize it and actually play it, you realize it's not...definitely an excellent adaptation of the Legendary system to embrace the theme of these beloved movies. Tense, frightening, lots of ways to vary up the play, whether you go straight through the movies or just mix and match objectives and characters. The added quirks like the 'Scan' mechanic rule, or the Chestbursters that get mixed into your deck when you fail to kill off a Facehugger; and there is always that uncertainty of what you drew from the Drone deck to mix with your Hives...amazing, really. I brushed it off at first but I am so glad I didn't in the end, because it is amazing.

RATING: 5
This is a rating of a 5-player play, which is the least (but still) recommended player count. I'd risk a theory that a game for 5 is just not working. There is no deck building in a game that has deck building in the title. Throughout the game I've manage to buy about 5-7 cards, while in the deck there still was 11 (out of starting 12) basic cards. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Marvel Legendary sounded pretty lame when I heard about it, but something about the Encounters:Alien stuff just seemed to take a luke-warm idea up to something that might just sizzle.

Turns out that was the case.  I picked this up on a lark and was surprised at how engrossing this co-op deck builder can be.  Plus it is difficult!  

I still have aspects of the game to explore (like hidden agendas and a mission set-up beyond "The Nostromo") but so far this game is a bona fide hit that really evokes the feeling of the source material.

A side note:  I'm not a fan of the comic-book style art on the cards and there is much about the layout that could have been changed for the sake of clarity and gameplay.  That said it's not enough to take away from what really is a great time!

RATING: 8.3
Although I am a superhero fan more that an aliens fan, I cannot but accept the superiority of this game. The theme invoked is realised in a way more concise and fulfilling  way than in the Marvel deckbuilder, I so much prefer the mat vs the board, even though the iconography could potentially be made in a better, more  clear way. But this is just nitpicking. I so dig this game!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[i]Posted: 5/9/16, Rated: 7[/i]

I like being open with you, and telling you when I want to like a game.  In the case of [i]Legendary Encounters: An Alien Deck Building Game (LE:A)[/i], I'm a big fan of the source material.  Not in the, "I could watch this every day for the rest of my life" sort of way, but in the, "It's been a couple of years since the last viewing and I'm craving me some [i]Alien[/i]" way.  The first movie was hella scary back in the day although it has lost must of its punch: its effects don't hold up well to HDTV's.  The second movie is just pure awesomeness.  The third and fourth movies if they were to exist are terrible.

On top of all that, I've been listening to the folks over at the [url=http://www.dicetower.com/game/146652/legendary-encounters-an-alien-deck-building-game]Dice Tower raving about the game[/url].  When [company=517]Upper Deck[/company] released [i][thing=174570][/thing][/i] and it could be combined with [i]LE:A[/i], I was finally in for a copy.  Alien vs. Predator is a concept that was best done in the original Dark Horse comic books, yielded two execrable films, and some fun video games.  I'm rambling at this point.  Let's get to the game.

[i]LE:A[/i] is the first cooperative deck-building game I've played.  Right there, that's interesting.  This isn't just "my engine is better than yours."  It's "we're working together to beat these baddies."  From helping each other buy better cards (the "Sergeant" card), to killing facehuggers before they turn into chestbursters inside of your teammates, to helping them kill bosses, this really feels like a team experience.  The "Coordinate" action is the source of this synergy, and I really like it.

[i]LE:A[/i] does a great job of translating the menace and the fear of the movies into a board game.  Those alien cards keep flowing into the Complex, and you won't know what's coming unless you spend combat points to "scan" that room, or until it shows up in the Combat Zone.  It's easy to keep those places separate because the game includes a playmat -- finally!  It makes managing the experience a breeze.

The artwork on the cards aren't movie stills, but rather comic-like pictures of scenes in the movies.  And here is my first gripe: some of the cards do a great job of depicting Ripley or Captain Dallas, while others are barely recognizable.  The pictures of Corporal Hicks and Private Hudson do not look anything like Michael Biehn or Bill Paxton.  Since the movies were sci-fi horror films, some of the artwork is graphically violent.  Also, there could have been a greater variety of artwork used.  All "Facehugger" cards use the exact same graphic -- even the ones that go into the Strike Deck (how you determine damage taken from the aliens) or the Drone Deck (extra baddies that are shuffled in with the cards for each objective).  I initially thought I was missing a card because I didn't know what to expect.

That leads me to the biggest gripe I have with this game: sorting it all out.  I had heard how onerous sorting was, but I didn't believe it until I tried it on my own.  [b]The instructions don't tell you how.[/b]  They leave it up to you to realize that there are deck identifiers on the bottom of each card written in a smaller, faint font.  If you're thinking about buying this game, then be sure to print out [filepage=107161]this card list[/filepage] by [user=gwarjuice]gwarjuice[/user].  It's a tremendous help to organizing the game.  Upper Deck should have included this information in the instruction booklet.

[i]Legendary Encounters: Alien[/i] delivers a tense, highly thematic experience.  Its tension and gruesome nature means I won't be playing this game all the time.  I rather expect a few weeks or months will pass, and then I'll be craving me some [i]Alien.[/i]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
(2-5 players, 60 min) The famous movie quadrilogy turned into a intensely creepy cooperative deckbuilding game. Play through each movie (or mix and match for new stories) recruiting your favorite characters as you stop the xenomorph infestations on LV-426, Fury 161, and the USM Auriga. Be careful not to get facehugged, or your life will become a ticking time bomb as the chestburster crawls its way to the top of your deck - and then it'll be all over.

RATING: 8
Am a huge Aliens fan, so this was a no-brainer. And I love it, even though I've only played, and will most likely only play, solo. As far as deck builders go, it holds my interest far better than the likes of Dominion and Ascension, but then it's a world I'm familiar with. I would like to see more card variations for sure, especially those used to build the Barracks deck. and there's a rather large luck component with regards to the Hive deck. I was able to crush the game on my third try simply because the Hive deck played in my favor throughout. In comparison, a card I needed as part of the win condition in an earlier attempt was at the bottom of the deck, leaving little chance I would have ever survived long enough to pull out a victory. Still, what hope should I have of winning anyway? They're frickin' acid-spitting, face-hugging aliens for crying out loud! Game over, man. Game over.

RATING: 6
A great theme game, but an only 'okay' deckbuilder. It really depends on what you want out of it. If you're looking for a fun game to bring to the table and a good theme, this is great. I suspect this has really awesome 'anyone-can-play' potential to bring friends into games. But it also depends what you want out of it. I like complicated deckbuilders and euro games. This is not Trains or Puzzle Strike. This is Flash Point or Pandemic: the deckbuilding game. The game often plays you, but there are definitely important decisions to be made. Overall though, my primary feeling was that a whole lot of this game was really chance based more than any amount of tactics or strategy. For a deckbuilding game, this isn't that deep, for a coop, I prefer Space Alert or Robinson Crusoe, but for a theme-drenched entry-level game that anyone can enjoy? This is pretty good.

RATING: 8

sleeved

Normally I'm not a big fan of pure deckbuilders.
Normally I'm not a fan of Co-Op games where you play multiplayer solo.
Normally I'm careful with games that recreate movies.

I was really happy with my Arctic Scavengers and I was fine with playing a round of Dominion with my spouse once in a while.
Then all of a sudden Legendary Encounters came along and I, as a big Alien (vs. Predator) fan, was ... interested.

When my replacement cards arrived (50 of the 600 were missprinted) I tried it...
...and fell in love with it.

Hell, yeah, I like this game. All the small details in the cards is so great. Fans will recognize so much...
And I was really surprised and happy as I scanned a room and unflipped Jonesy.

I am a bit afraid though that it might get dull after time passes by but help is on it's way. The predator box might cure that itch.

Nevertheless I'm looking forward to playing much much more of this.

RATING: 7.15
This is a good game but I'm not sure if it's a great game.  It is highly thematic despite its roots in the Legendary system.  Really dig the scanning mechanics and the objective/hive deck system.  Brings out the flavor immensely.

Nitpicky complaints include the fact that this still has a long setup/teardown time, the card backs mimicking Legendary's are ugly for this theme and detract from the playmat, and the constant shuffling/rote tasks detract from solo play when running multiple characters.  

Still, overall this is a keeper.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
So first off: my boyfriend and I played through all four scenarios over the course of two evenings and won every one on the first try. Which brings me to my personal feelings on scenario-based games, which are completely arbitrary. 

So on the one hand it's neat to play a co-op game with these very designed challenges - having been an avid video game my whole life it is a familiar warm and fuzzy sort of feeling. And it's worth saying that this game would be nowhere near as interesting without the scenarios. They are much of the appeal of the game, and each one feels very, very unique which is really cool!

But on the other, whenever I complete all of the available scenarios for a game like this, I feel like I've "beaten" it and do not feel compelled to replay them or start making my own. Especially in this instance, where it's pretty clear that making your own won't increase the difficulty (which in the case of us beating all of them on the first try, is something this sorely needs to make me want to replay it). So for me: four games worth of content feels extremely slim for something so large and pricey.

I would be interested to try the traitor variant, which should make it harder and sufficiently change things up... but again I suspect I would probably only care to beat each of the four challenges again with a traitor. 

The alien player module is also a cool idea, but neither of us ever even died so I definitely won't be replaying just for that.

As for the game itself I'll put it this way: I enjoyed this more as a co-op game than as a deckbuilder. As a deckbuilder, there are very few options to prune your deck (it's basically scenario-dependent) and when combined with the fact that you can get stuck with a bunch of cards in the market that nobody wants it feels pretty lackluster compared to other games in the genre. An option to clear the market really feels like it should have been included.

But as a co-op the game presents some pretty fun challenges to overcome. The game is always engaging and there's a lot of tension - particularly around the scan mechanic which really hits that risk/reward sweet spot. The coordinate cards are a really nice touch and a great way to make you feel like you're working as a team. Largely this would be the same game solo, so it's nice to have that extra small mechanic.

I've mulled over the game's difficulty (or lack thereof?) a lot. I think it boils down to the fact that it seems to have taken the Ghost Stories route of difficulty where enemies can chain together in devastating and unexpected ways, but once you're familiar with the deck it's much easier to plan for. Though it feels a little better balanced here, where you can probably see a new enemy type and live to fight another turn.

I'll also say that I did not expect for the theme to be as engaging as it was. Once we were done, I immediately went and rewatched Alien. The cards and everything are very thoughtfully themed, but really the fact that this a game where the enemy is always creeping closer and you can never, ever dally is what takes it home. Even as a big fan of the first film, I tend not to care about licensed IP games so this was a very pleasant surprise in that respect.

So at the end of the day this is a fun game that I find hard to recommend buying. If you're personally not averse to replaying scenarios or making your own (even if they're not going to be more difficult), then sure pick it up. Otherwise... I don't know, maybe split the cost of a copy with your group and pass it around between all the couples or something.

As for me, I'm glad I didn't have to buy this. I got four games out of it, and at most I may get four more. We'll see.

Edit: oh and one more thing, but while I dig that this has the Star Realms-esque faction/alliance/whatever it's called in this one system I found its presentation poor - it was very easy for me to miss the ally required symbol on an ability. I wish they were visually separated into normal ability / faction ability like they are in Star Realms.

RATING: 9
A few fairly simple changes to the Legendary formula (such as full co-op, enemy cards staying face down until 'scanned' or about to attack you, the co-ordinate ability on some cards) make a much bigger impact than you'd think. The theme here is spot on - for example, you have the option to scan aliens and other hazards as they approach, and you can actually get impregnated by a facehugger if you're unlucky or reckless. In a stroke of genius, this is represented by a chestburster card being placed in your discard pile. When this card ends up in your hand in a future turn, well...that's it for you. Unless you or one of your buddies can trash the card beforehand, that is.

There are a few things I'm not keen on, though. The alien player (which comes into effect when someone is taken out by a chestburster - another clever touch) more-or-less plays on autopilot and is a bit too deadly. There is also player elimination in this game - a turn-off for me, but thankfully there are unofficial variants that address this nicely.

RATING: 8
Medium weight deckbuilder with emphasis on theme and player cooperation. The decisions are many times obvious to seasoned gamers, and can take a bit of time to set up, but when it comes to being enjoyable and tied to its theme, it's up there with the best. The wrench in the machinery are that the available card display can get clogged up so you need to balance deck efficiency with the need to see more cards, and I simply love that. It changes the game from a strict deck efficiency puzzle to a probabilistic min-max one. The other thing is that some of the cards are really cool and clever (facehugger anyone?) and that made me smile when I first encountered them. Lastly, the PvP option and hidden agendas variant, as well as the movie seanario progression, kick the package a notch up.

Overall, a very enjoyable and solid design, and one I will most definitely revisit quite a lot. Recommended.

+ Highly thematic and engaging
+ Easy to teach and with quite a smooth gameplay
+ Highly cooperative
+ The clogging up of the card display presents a nice twist
+ There is a lot to be explored between different movies, variants, characters...
+ Great components and art
+ Understandable rulebook

= Can have early player elimination in extreme circumstances
= Can be easy with 2 players (but you can take it up a notch with houserules)

- Can take  a bit of time to setup
- Buying it new (I didn't) results in a long chore of putting the decks together

RATING: 4
Too much luck involved with this game. Luck with the character draw deck, the hive draw deck, and your own deck. Other games have more mitigation for this like Mage Knight does. You can easily look at your character deck after losing and see all the "good cards". All cards should basically be good, just how you use them should matter. Others say 2 players is easiest, but from the play throughs on youtube and my experience I'd disagree. 4 players I have not tried.

Also, don't see this as a non-solo game due to lack of decisions.  Not a very good game IMO. When you finally win you don't feel like trying it again. You feel like playing each movie/scenario until you win and then putting it away never to be taken out again.

RATING: 10
A Marveles verziót ismertem, és nagyon, de tényleg nagyon szerettem, mégis, annak ellen tudtam állni (ami köszönhető volt annak a szomorú ténynek is, hogy a főellenségek és karakterek egyetlen rajzot kaptak, ami a játékélménybe is belerondított). Aztán kijött ez az Alienes, továbbfejlesztett verzió, és nem bírtam tovább, beszereztem.

Egyetlen, két fős játék után azonnali 10 pontot adtam neki: egyszerűen ez a játék így tökéletes. Miért? Ha már 10 pontot adtam, 10 pontba foglalom:
1. A playmat (játéktábla, vászonból) csúcsszuper, mondhatni überfasza.
2. Végre minden más tulajdonságú kártya más-más, de csodaszép grafikát kapott.
3. Nem hiányzik belőle semmi, nem kíván kiegészítőt, így is tökéletesen teljes játék.
4. Fantasztikus antológia az Alien sorozathoz: mind a 4 film végigjátszható (persze akár keverni is lehet a dolgokat).
5. Az Alien-hangulat (és az ezzel járó játékfeszültség) 100%-os. Egy kis hátborzongató zene a háttérbe és néhány Alienke meg tojáska az űrhajón és garantált a cidri.
6. A játékosoknak van beleszólásuk egymás körébe (ez újdonság a Marveles verzióhoz képest). Ezzel nem csak a kooperációt erősítették fel, de ahhoz is hozzájárultak, hogy ne legyen holtidő, hiszen így állandóan figyelni kell saját lapunkat, tudunk-e vajon segíteni.
7. Egy másik újdonság: az ellenségeket szkennelni kell, amire újabb harci erőt kell szánni, ez pedig izgalmat és kíváncsiságot csempész a dologba, miközben meg is nehezíti a játékosok dolgát.
8. A sérülések nem szokványos módon érkeznek, az erre kialakított pakli rendkívül ötletes kártyákkal van ellátva.
9. A 16 különböző karakter (4-4 minden filmből), a 10 szerepkártya akiket megtestesítünk, a 4 helyszín (melyből minden játékban 1 van jelen), a 12 célkártya (melyből mindig 3 van játékban) és a drón dekk akkora változatosságot ad a játéknak, ami garantálja, hogy ne játsszuk ki pár nap alatt és ne unjunk rá egyhamar.
10. Mert egyszerű a szabály, mert könnyen megérthető és ennek ellenére mégis komplex.

Számomra az eddigi TOP1 deckbuilding építő játék amivel valaha játszottam! (És remélem ez a véleényem megmarad későbbi játékok után is, hisz mint mondtam, eddig csak 1 partin vagyunk túl... de holnap jön a következő! :) )

Beszerzés: 2015. január

RATING: 6.5
I enjoyed this game the first three times I played it, but my interest has waned rapidly thereafter. To my mind, this just reduces the game to a random outcome, relying on the order of card appearance from multiple decks.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.8
Legendary Encounters is an amazing cooperative deck-building game. If you are a fan of the Alien(s) movies, this is a must-have. The game design incorporates a number of improvements and refinements over Marvel Legendary. Each player has an avatar and a personalized starting deck. That's a nice improvement. I also like how the Hive deck ramps up in difficulty as you progress through the objectives. The objectives also provide some variety into the gameplay. Scanning to see what the enemies are is brilliantly thematic and adds tension to the gameplay. The ability to "Coordinate" is amazing and really adds to the cooperative nature of the game. It practically eliminates any downtime since you are involved on everyone's turn. The fact that the game is fully cooperative (when you don't incorporate the secret goals or traitor variant) isn't necessarily an improvement over Marvel Legendary, but it can be with the right group. Where the game suffers (compared to Marvel Legendary) is player elimination, unfortunately. It's no fun for your character to be killed and you have to watch the other players play. There are proposed house rules for eliminating the player elimination, but I haven't tried them yet. Having a chestbursted player turn into an Alien and play an Alien deck mitigates this somewhat, but only slightly since it's more likely that a player dies from strikes than a chestburster, and playing as an Alien simply isn't very fun. The game also currently suffers from the lack of replayability compared to Marvel Legendary's near infinite replayability. I just don't think it makes sense thematically to play scenarios that don't match up with one of the movies. I can't see ever mixing characters and movie objectives. Ultimately, I think I will get tired of playing the same movie scenarios more than a few times each, but, for now, I love it. It's possible the planned expansion could significantly improve the replayability. I hope so. As with Marvel Legendary, the game does not scale well with the number of players. The sweet spot seems to be 3 players. Do not play with 5 players unless you do a couple rounds of recruiting first. Solo play doesn't seem as well implemented as Marvel Legendary. The artwork is very uneven. It ranges from superb for the Aliens to rather poor for some of the characters.

The above comes across as more negative than I actually feel about the game. It's a really great cooperative and a lot of fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A solid thematic deck builder, bringing the Alien quadrilogy to the table.

A cooperative game, this allows the players to work together to take on the iconic Aliens, complete the objectives from the films and try to survive.

I find the Legendary: Encounters games to be better than the Marvel Legendary game, as they're actually cooperative. Alien has a team of players fighting a common threat, Marvel feels more like individual heroes who happen to be fighting the same fight.

Alien also brings individual roles giving the players different abilities, a traitor mechanic and event the possibility of a player dying due to a Chestburster and becoming an Alien!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
What they’ve made here via the deckbuilding mechanism is a classic solo/coop adventure game. You fight bad guys, level up, then fight tougher bad guys until you either complete the game’s victory conditions or they wipe you out. The entire arc of fight-upgrade-fight while telling a story and applying appropriately increased tension is all here, and it’s all perfectly balanced and tuned. 

The key facet of the game is this enemy deck and track. The deck is made up of three tranches of cards that get increasingly harder (as in any good adventure game). Each turn a card is added facedown to the enemy track, pushing any cards there closer down to the combat zone (where they auto-activate). Events and hazards also come down this track and trigger different effects based on the location you’re playing (based on the movie) and the current objective card (you have to get through 3 objectives each game to win). 

You can spend your actions to scan (ie, flip over) cards in the track. Revealed enemies can be attacked. The events and hazards either outright hurt you or mess with your plans and provide a lot of variety for each section of each game in a simple and effective way. The facedown element provides a simple and nice fog of war and tension. The scaling works very well and by the time you’re in the bottom part of the enemy deck, you’re actually pretty badass. 

What takes it to another level of enjoyment for me is the way theme is incorporated into the game. Characters and situations and even quotes are made into cards. So you can actually have Jonesy the Cat or cute lil’ Newt as a card in your deck. "She'll breed. You'll die." is an Objective. Assuming you’re a fan of the genre, this works very well and all my friends have expressed delight flipping a card to find something memorable. 

Here’s one example of theme rendered well here: if you get a Facehugger attached to you, you have your turn and the next player’s turn to defeat it or you add a Chestburster card to your discard pile. When the Chestburster card is eventually drawn, you “suffer great pain and die.” You can become an alien player playing against the other players if you want to play that mode, otherwise, yeah, there is potential player elimination. Hey, you saw the movie; these things mean business.

I don’t want to oversell it. It falls in the light-to-medium category for depth of decisions but I find the overall package of depth, theme, and balance to be a great combination. They’ve hit on a rather simple system that lends itself to playing out a story very well. In fact, from what I’ve heard there are other franchises in the queue (Predator next and possibly Firefly at some point). If you're at all a fan of the Alien theme, consider this a must-have (or at least must-try). 

Caveat: the cards come all mixed up in a "52 pickup" kind of way. Print the card manifest from the Files section and set aside some time. I strongly printing custom dividers that several people have created.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9

I dislike:

Final verdict: As with the Predator version, but I'm not sure I can say which is the better game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Let me start off by saying that this game is perfect for ME. So, if you are like me, you will love this game. If that's good enough for you, stop what you're doing and buy it.

Reasons this game is perfect for me: 
1. I am a huge film buff. I love movies, including the Alien franchise. Even the wacky fourth one that is confusing and weird.
2. I love challenging games. "Oh, we lost?... LET'S PLAY AGAIN!"
3. I am an gracious alpha gamer. I see all the best moves and know what we should do. In this game 85% of the time, there is a definite best move and a definite best way to play your hand. To make the game fun for everyone playing though, I allow mistakes, I let them play the game and I hold my breath. It makes it fun, cause guess what, if you're on a ship and aliens show up, you might make a mistake too.
4. I like 2 hour games. This game says 45 min... I haven't played a game in under 1 hour  yet, which I love. Great length.
5. I love co-op games. I used to HATE co-op games, now I LOVE them (good ones). I grew up yelling, fighting, blaming, complaining, during board games with my family because someone did something that hurt someones feelings... blah, blah, blah. So, co-op games for my family are a lifesaver.

Walk with me. I was researching games one day and felt convinced I would love this game. I didn't have the cash though so I called up my bro and told him to buy it... unfortunately, I knew he wouldn't love the theme or how difficult it was. BUT, what's this... Legendary Marvel. Boom. He bought the game one Thanksgiving and we all loved it. It was great. There were and are some problems with it though (for me).

Problems with Legendary: Marvel:
1. The bad guys escape and.... nothing happens. Most of the time it doesn't change anything and sometimes it can help you when the bad guys escape?! What? That literally doesn't make any sense.
2. It's a co-op game... that you're competing in? Why did they add those stupid victory points? The end game feels like this, "Yay! We won!" - me... "No, I did." - silly person who got most victory points... 
3. Because of the victory points, that changes what you buy and who you kill and thus fights can happen because "You're being selfish for doing that! Do this!" ... " But I want this..." "All you care about is yourself." This exchange happens often in Marvel.

Well, guess what ladies and gents. That's right. Legendary Encounters fixes all those problems with flying colors.

Things that make Legendary: Encounters the BEST themed game ever:
1. The enemy cards come out face down. Why? CAUSE YOU CAN'T SEE THEM! They are running around in your ship and you'll only see them when you scan the room they are in. Genius.
2. When the enemy cards leave the Complex (in Marvel this is when the enemy "escapes") they come into the Combat Zone and you have to fight them. If you don't kill them you take damage and lose health. You only have limited health.
3. There are Coordinate cards. These make the game fantastic. The more players you play with, the quicker aliens come out. (It's math. Just trust me.) So, the game gives us Coordinate cards to help with that problem. The Coordinate cards really help with the teamwork aspect and adds another layer of fun.
4. When you have 1 health left, you're scared. You are genuinely fearing for your life. "Should I scan the room? What if I get a strike?!" "MEDIC!!! Someone heal me!"

Even if you die, the game is fun. Then you're rooting on your teammate and still advising on decisions. The very first game we played (which we played entirely wrong, which in turn made the game impossible at times. I'll explain later) was my friend, wife, and myself. We literally only won because my wife died. If she hadn't we would have all lost. But since she died, my friend got to go and he had enough damage to kill it. That was an amazing event that we still occasionally bring up.

At this point, I hope you are convinced. Buy the game. This is really the end of the review. But, for you who want to hear how you can totally mess the game up, continue reading.

Rules are important. Words are important.
Well, I read the rulebook and thought I understood the game.
I took the objective 1, 2, and 3 cards and shuffled them together to be our Hive deck. We also only had the # of Drone cards as # of people (It's actually the # of people x's 3). DON'T DO THIS! What this resulted in was 15+ games with minimal (like 3) wins. And when we did, it was SO HARD! We ended up having to keep the Main Alien in the complex for the whole game. Since we couldn't kill it till we had accomplished the first 2 objectives, we just had to pray that we would draw the other objective cards before we died. This was very hard. In the rules it says something like, "If the main alien gets there before the 2nd objective is completed, good luck" and that sentence formed in my brain the way I thought we had to play. Lol. I played many solo games to figure out how to make the game winnable. Then, my brother in law, bought the game, read the rules, and told me. Oh, my goodness. We have only lost 1 time since. So the game has gotten much easier. 

If any of you guys out there are wanting a tough, challenging, thrilling, rollercoaster of impending doom, I implore you to shuffle all the Hive cards together (with only the # of Drone cards as # of people) and give it a whirl.

RATING: 4
As with the base game of Legendary, a really good idea but execution is poor.

This particular set of stand alone cards is based upon the four alien movies, but uses the same mechanics of the legendary game. 

The little symbols upon the cards that are needed to kick off the special abilities of card you play later in the turn are simply too small, and frankly quite irrelevant. The majority of the aliens are 3-4 strength to kill which can be achieved very easily. The river of cards you can buy into your deck seems to be full of repeat cards so essentially you build a one trick pony deck. i.e. it does this and this alone. YAY :shake:

The coordinate is a nice mechanic. I can play coordinate cards in other players turns to give then the buying power or damage from the card and then draw a replacement. Unfortunately the replacement you draw is generally not going to be as good as the coordinate card you played therefore you jeopardise your own turn.

RATING: 9
This is the ultimate deck-building game IMO.  It's fully cooperative, and the group truly feels like it is struggling together to stay alive.  It is this difficulty that keeps the tension and interest up, but the game also gives you several options for lowering or raising the difficulty as needed to match your mood.

I also have to say that, like Friday, this is an excellent solo deck-building game as long as you're willing to manage two player decks as this game does not work well with just one player deck.  In fact, the players' greatest strength (coordinating) doesn't exist with just one player deck.

Finally, I highly recommend investing in some good dividers.  Justin Hiltz produced an excellent set that I happily paid a local printer $30 to print on high quality, glossy card stock and it helps greatly with the setup and breakdown times, which can be daunting, but very worth it.

RATING: 7
I was expecting an extremely thematic deckbuilder along the lines of Thunderstone (which was my impression after reading about the slowly advancing enemies before bursting through). What I got was an often (but not always) thematic deckbuilder along the lines of Ascension. I'm not a fan of the Ascension system as a whole. It was some fun when I first got the app and played a bunch of games, but became quite stale once you tire of the luck of the draw and the "most expensive card is the best" deterministic draft. Legendary Encounters: Aliens is a better game than Ascension as the theme does come through much better. However, it is still just a deckbuilder with card effects that serve the constructs of the game more than the establishment of a narrative. Again, that's fine, but it didn't meet the expectations I had built up based on the reviews of others. Still, I think it's a fine game and it's nice to have a co-op of this sort. There's a good amount of tension that is built up. But at the end of the day the game is still weighted heavily on luck of the draw, and playing your cards down pretty much determines which alien you can kill and what you can buy. There's very little thinking behind it. There are little moments for ingenious play, and so I appreciate that. If that aspect wasn't there, I would have probably rated this the same as Ascension.

RATING: 8
Very well done, with lots of tension that definitely builds up over the course of the game. Certainly feels like Aliens, thematically.

As a cooperative game, it works much better than the original Legendary. The original had almost no ability for the players to actually work together, so whether or not you beat the Villain was not based on how the team worked together. But here, with the new Coordinate mechanic, you have lots of opportunities to feel like you are working together. The decisions aren't as much of a puzzle as other coops like Pandemic, but you still get the feeling of cooperating.

We've stopped using the secret roles, though. Being evil is just not very fun or interesting, as you don't have many options to undermine the rest of the party.
Being the Alien player is fun, though.

RATING: 9.5
I am not a fan of Legendary not really a fan of deck builders, but this game is a huge improvement from Legendary.  Theme is paramount, the plot of the game literary follows the story's of the 4 movies to a tea, and the mechanics of the game fit perfectly in with the theme.  Face huggers, the Queen, Jonesy, Ash, Burke, Bishop, all worked into the game in interesting and thematic ways, that make sense.  With just enough randomness, each time you play, things happen in different and interesting ways.  Recruiting cards is strategic as there are powerful combos that you can try to put together. 

This is simply the best co-op game I know of, hands down.  Players must work together and play cards that help other players.  Play is tense and interesting.  You can even play with a trader, or as an Alien with the optional rules.  Tons of replayability with the 4 different movie decks and the 16 character decks which could be mixed together for all kinds of wild adventures.

I played this game with 2 players that are not even fans of the movies (one had never even seen them) and they liked it so much we played twice more after the first game.  

If you are fan of the movies this is a must have, even if your not and you like deck building or Co-op you have to give it a try.

RATING: 9
A pakliépítés neve: Halál
Baráti társaságban sikerült kipróbálnom a játékot, ahol is szétrobbanó mellkassal végeztem a padlón. :) 
Nagy kedvencem a filmsorozat minden része (igen, még a 3. és 4. epizód is), így nagy kedvvel fogtam neki a játék megismerésének (örök élmény, amikor kedves amerikai barátainknak elmondtuk, hogy is került fordításra az első 3 film címe szóról szóra, és a reakció: whaaaaaaaat?). Természetesen itt sem feltétel a filmek megnézése, azonban rengeteget ad a játékhoz (úgy érzem, tipikusan rajongók részére készült játékról van szó). Na meg nem is olyan nagy ügy 3-4 jó film megtekintése a megszokott szappanoperák és híradó helyett. :)
Alapvetően a 4 film története elevenedik meg a kártyákon, miközben a játékosok az életükért küzdve próbálják megoldani a különböző feladatokat. Kártyáink kijátszásával új karaktereket toborozhatunk vagy sérüléseket okozhatunk saját körünkben (plusz egyéb hatások is segíthetik túlélésünket). Egyes kártyák lehetővé teszik segítségnyújtást más játékos körében is. Ezek kiemelt szerepet játszanak, mivel a játékos köre végén eldobja a megmaradt lapjait és mindig új „kezet” húz fel (összesen 6 lapot), tehát egyes nehéz feladatokhoz/ellenfelekhez bizony segíteni kell egymást.
Alapvető taktika az Őrmester beszerzése (klasszikus magyar szinkronban: „Nézz meg a szemfenekem!”, máig nem tudom elfelejteni.
A karakterek közül eddig leghasznosabb számomra a gyógyító képességű volt, szó szerint életeket tudsz menteni vele.
Mint minden pakliépítős játéknál, itt is minél jobban megismered a lapokat, annál jobb paklit építesz fel, jobb kombinációkat használsz és ennek megfelelő lapokat vásárolsz.
A játékban annak nehézségét szabályozhatod (normál módon is kihívás a küldetés teljesítése), a filmek végigjátszása mellett a későbbiekben keverheted a helyszíneket, küldetéseket, karaktereket kényedre-kedvedre. Sőt érdemes kipróbálni a full Ripley paklival való ténykedést is (bár azzal eddig egyetlen egyszer sem sikerült nyernem – mire szépen „muzsikálni” kezdett a pakli, egyszerűen kihaltam a pályáról).
Sokak számára furcsa lehet, hogy egy társasjátékot szólóban játszol, de ez arra is alkalmas, sőt nagyon kellemes tapasztalat, így magányos farkasoknak is bátran ajánlható.
Játszható áruló humán karakterrel is, valamint akár egy idegen harcost is irányíthatunk a játék során a többiek életének megnehezítésére.
Ha van kedved, háttérzenének hallgasd az adott film zenéjét. Külön élmény!
Itt már várom a kiegészítőt is az új karakterekkel, esetleg a Prometeus küldetéssel.

RATING: 8
I like deckbuilders in general, and this one has some interesting twists. The board/playmat is a little busy, with lots of things to track. However, I was very surprised by how thematic this game felt. As a huge fan of the property on which it is based, I loved the way playing it felt. Different sets of cards really provide different feelings of play, much like the movies on which they are based. This really demands to be played with people who love deckbuilding games and also love the Alien movies. Without really liking both of those things, I could see this falling a little flat. I happen to be in that core audience, but my suspicion is that I would end up enjoying this a lot more than most of the other people I would get to play it with.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4

This is my biggest disappointment in 2015. Not just boardgame disappointments but like, this might be the worst thing that happened to me this year in general. This game is awful.


Pros:

- The artwork is gory and over the top and I'm a big fan. I'm really glad they didn't use stills from the movie as this always comes off as cheesy and reminds me of the sad games I used to play in the 80's.

- The game comes with dividers to section out the cards. They're just plain Jane and have no artwork or titles on them but still, that's pretty cool.

- LE: Alien does invoke a sense of urgency but it's not thematically integrated as well as Arkham Horror nor does it induce as much panic as the better State of Siege games.

- ......yeah that's all I can think of. Okay get ready because this next part is going to be pretty big.

Cons:

- The game comes in a big box that is about 50% air. You can sleeve all your cards and they occupy the better part of one side of the box. I initially thought that this was to accommodate the multiple expansions coming out but I hear more rumours of new Legendary Encounter stand alone games than I do expansions for existing games.

- The setup and tear down of this game takes too long for what it's worth. There is a lot of shuffling different decks together before you start the game and separating decks after the game is over. And remember that oversized box? Once you take out the required cards you need for your game, the cards remaining in the box seem to slip and slide under the cheap foam dividers which infuriated me to no end. Setting up, organizing and tearing down is a game unto itself.

- I take issue with this labeling itself as a deckbuilder as this is more of a card drafter. You start the game with 13 cards, 12 of them being shitty 1 point cards and you're stuck with them for the rest of the game. Options do come up during the game to get rid of a card but these are few and far between and I only mention it to appease the defenders of this game. So there's no deck pruning mechanism which takes a good amount of control away from you in terms of building your deck. Secondly, you buy cards and place them in your deck but these cards tend to be the same ten cards over and over with a rare popping up now and then. It's a very boring and constrictive mechanism.

- There is barely any player interaction. You play cards from your hand and if another player decides to, he can play a card during your turn that says "Coordinate" to add the points on that card to your point total.

- There is no tough decision making. There are choices but they all seem obvious and also during your turn you have 2 choices. Play strikes to kill something or play recruit points to buy a card. I won't get into room scanning here for length purposes, but paying to flip a card is pretty much all it is.

- Player elimination. I have seen a person die on the second round and had to sit out the rest of the game. There is no reason that boardgames today use this tired old mechanism. Nothing kills the enjoyment of a game more than this mechanism.

- The traitor rules seem tacked on at the last minute as if the developer wanted a traitor mechanism because "traitor games are hot right now".

- The whole game's ruleset just seems half finished and too open ended for no real reason. It's like they tried to cram everything into the game and thereby took away any semblance of elegance, personality or uniqueness.


I could go on about how the movies all feel the same. How every game is just flipping cards and playing strikes until you flip the objective card. How quickly the game grows stale. How little strategy is involved, how badly it scales, how face huggers and chest bursters could have been so much better but I want to keep this somewhat short. Anyway, this is a terrible game and shouldn't be in the top 50 thematic games let alone the top ten. The good news is I can quickly see this game taking a big fall over the next few years.

4/10

[i]Any comments on this review can be left here [geeklist=192221][/geeklist][/i]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
Rating after 10 games, averaging about 60 minutes per game.

Will undoubtedly be the best DBG of 2014.

Game mat comes with the game; finally someone who understands the advantage of a mat over a board!

The first scenario was the most difficult for us, and our sweet spot was to add 1 Drone card per player +1.

A great enhancement on the Legendary system!!  Mechanically flawless, scales well, enjoyable, and brimming with theme.

The "coordination" mechanic adds to the Coop nature of the game.  You are picking up cards which will assist your teammates, and playing one on their turn is necessary more often than not.

The added need to scan for enemies really adds to this game, and plays well with the theme.  Once in the Combat Zone, you get attacked by each enemy present.  Nice!

Giving the "3" strength Sergeants "Coordinate" and a Character Class is brilliant!  Even low cost cards give you pause for consideration, depending on how you want to structure your deck.

Wounds do not clutter your deck, they accumulate besides your character until you are eliminated.  Player elimination is mitigated by the Alien player additional rule, which essentially ensures the game will end much quicker, so you can start a new one.  ;)

Although a 10 strength Alien is frightening, the worst enemy is the darn Facehugger!! "Ok, before scanning, be sure to keep at least 3 attack points in case you reveal a Facehugger !!!"


Only negative thing I can find... The name on each card indicating which deck they belong to is way too small... for me anyways.

At least one person I know picked up a copy with 50 duplicate cards...  A slight assembly error, which the publisher immediately recognized and advised would be sending the missing cards (within the next 3 weeks).

Looking forward to trying this with the traitor rules!! The added angst must be exhilarating!

RATING: 7
[b]After 6 plays:[/b]  I want to give this an 8 in the worst way—and I often come by here to do just that—but something's holding me back.

I don't know if it's the player elimination—not something I normally have a problem with, as usually when people start dying the rest of the living aren't far behind, but sometimes one person will kick out early and for whatever reason the game will suddenly let up and enter a weird glide phase where things actually turn around, leaving the dead player with little to do other than dealing cards and sliding them around on the playmat forlornly.*

Or maybe it's that fragile variability where the card draws from the myriad decks conspire to make the game stutter between laughably easy and impossibly hard, with little rhyme or reason between either state.

It feels like it [i]wants[/i] to be a story game, but all the moving parts detract from that—and it's too swingy to function as a strategy game, stranding it in an ultimately unsatisfying limbo between the two.  It does neither well enough to really shine.

Also, the card art is hideously inconsistent, scribbling all over the map from cool/evocative to WTF/amateurish.

[size=7]*I suppose the "Player Aliens" advanced rule would solve this for those who die by chestburster, effectively accelerating the end, but what about the poor sap who died by other means?  And yeah, it's easy enough to houserule it so everyone who dies plays an alien, but that just feels like piling on... but maybe that's the whole point, right?  The only problem is that I'm violently allergic to houserules.[/size]

Pro: 
*Fun.

Cons:
*Too much luck: some games are a cake walk, while others are impossible. 
*Worst card stock for a game with lots of shuffling I've ever played with. One of my two "Somebody help!" cards from the strike deck was torn at the bottom right between what looks like small depressions made by metal clamps - I emailed UD, who made me jump thru some hoops but then mailed me a replacement.

Minor nitpicks:
*The theme doesn't work when playing with only the 1st or 3rd movies' cards because there aren't soldiers or multiple aliens in them.
*I'd've preferred photos from the movies instead of cartoon art.

RATING: N/A
Like the original Legendary it is a pain to set up and put away. The way the bad things work has changed to introduce a Strike deck as well as the concept of hit points. Which allows player elimination. The ability to give some cards to other players in their turn and to heal other players makes the game more cooperative. The scheme and master mind have been replaced by scenarios and objectives. The way the bad cards come out face down and are only revealed as they leave the first 5 spaces and move into the combat area gives a feeling of the Alien movies. 

In terms of production values the cards looks too similar to each other and the text seems even smaller than the original game. It still doesn't have named dividers. It has a rubber play mat which is good.

RATING: 2.5
My first couple games were great, but in general the game seems to be incredibly uneven. Too many games wind up with the mid-game and on being completely stressless. Yet you still have to keep playing through because you can't finish until you complete the objective in the last deck, which may not be possible until you've drawn the very last card of the alien deck. So you just spin your wheels. The worst bit is that, if you're unlucky, a facehugger at the wrong time can simply kill somebody. Usually avoidable, but when it happens it feels cheap. And when you're playing 2-player, it basically just ends the game in an anti-climactic loss, because even if you could win by playing through, it's incredibly tedious for the surviving player and boring for the deceased player to do so.

I loved this at the beginning, but now it's on the trade pile. Super disappointing, because I was so pumped when I ordered it. Game's rating dropped from an 8 after 2 players to a 4 after about 5 or 6. Boo.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I'm not a fan of the player elimination (which can occur on a player's second turn). While it serves as a motivating threat and fits the theme well, 30+ minutes removed from the game is obnoxious.

Some bits of the Legendary system irk me as well. It's a little too simple for me, and the limitations on card availability and deck-pruning are frustrating. For folks who are familiar with deck-building games, be warned that the only way you can weed-out cards is through card effects - no trashing as an action! Drawing an entire hand of starter cards during the endgame is super lame, I must admit.

Adherence to theme, on the other hand, is excellent. Face-down threats progress every turn as you urgently strengthen your deck. Most matches felt hopeless, but the few narrow victories were worth the struggle.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I had never played any of the Legendary game system before this. The box comes with card configurations to support playing versions around each of the first 4 alien films. After that, you can mix and match characters and objectives from the four movies to experience many alternate reality Alien films. Players are working together to defeat the Alien deck, which is comprised of three mini decks stacked on each other for objectives 1-3. The requirements for each objective is contained within its mini deck and be a simple as turning over a couple of cards to defeating incredibly difficult aliens in very specific circumstances that you usually need other cards to achieve. The alien deck is revealed slowly with face-down cards traveling through "The Complex" until reaching a combat zone where aliens can attack the players. As such, players are trying to reveal and take cards out of play while in The Complex before they have the ability to attack.

On a player's turn, she can fight any face-up aliens, scan The Complex in order to reveal the cards there or purchase a more powerful crew member to add to their decks. Players begin with very basic fight and purchase cards and need to improve pretty quick. Because many objectives are dependent on drawing certain cards, you have to be prepared to last through a spell of not getting the cards that will help you. A unique aspect to this game (and I assume all Legendary titles) is the "coordinate" ability. Cards with coordinate allow you to give their ability to another player while you draw another card. I have not seen another game with this ability and it really contributes well to the co-op intention of the designers. Because cards are drawn in a certain order, you are certainly at the mercy of the shuffle to a significant extent. If that doesn't bother you, then you'll find a good, tense, thematic game where seriously f'd up crap awaits with every flip of the card...

RATING: 7
Read rules Sept 24 2014

This is largely the same game as Legendary, which in my opinion is very disappointing. Legendary is an okay game with some almost clever ideas so I was really hoping this iteration would step it up a notch or two. 

However, there are some positive changes. The game can now be played full co-op which is a definite improvement. Hopefully the game is more difficult. They have introduced some mechanics to help one another which should help the co-op feel come through. They also have a much smoother difficulty knob in the Drone cards so making the game harder should be easy.

It's also worth noting that given the similarity to Legendary they did an admirable job implementing the theme.

RATING: 9.5
Wow!  This game is a blast!  I adore the Alien movies (especially the first two), so this definitely grabbed my interest.  I do like deck building and co-op as mechanisms, so I did my research and scooped this one up without playing it first.  I made a good move.  Such a fun game!  It is dripping with theme.  You will feel the dread as you draw strikes or move new aliens down the complex to meet you in the combat zone.  It also can be played solo, which is a nice plus.  I understand that common opinion is that this is superior to the Marvel game, but I haven't tried that yet.  I don't really have interest in the Marvel theme, so this game was meant for me.  Do be warned that sorting the (600) cards the first time will take some time and there are sometimes missing cards.  I was missing one card and had to get UpperDeck to send it to me.  The individual card checklist found here on BGG is a necessity.  If you can get past those hurdles, the game is fantastic!  Best deck-builder that I have played.

RATING: 6
Revendu.
Au premier contact, le jeu impressionne par la règle du Chestburster: Si vous récupérez un Facehugger, si il n'a pas était éliminé avant la fin de votre prochain tour vous devez piocher une carte chestburster et la mettre dans votre défausse. Arrivé à la fin de votre pioche, vous mélangez votre défausse qui redevient votre pioche. Si vous piochez le chestburster... GameOver!
Il est donc facile d'imaginer à quelle point cette règle créée une importante tension dans la partie dès qu'elle se déclenche. Malheureusement cette règle implique aussi que, si vous disposer de trop de cartes vous permettant de bannir des cartes de votre jeu (carte de la main de départ par exemple),  le chestburster sera trop facilement éliminé est ne sera donc plus un élément de tension. Du coup il est très compliqué de gérer la taille de sa pioche, ce qui engendre des moments ou on se refuse à acheter de nouvelles cartes  par ce que notre jeu est déjà bien assez épais  et que toutes vos bonnes cartes sont fonduent au milieu de la main de base et de quelques autres cartes de transition dont on aimerait bien se délester... Cette fausse bonne idée engendre aussi du coup une difficulté assez brutal du jeu. Difficulté qui s'amplifiera si vous mourrez et que vous prenez le deck Alien pour pourrir votre/vos ex partenaire(s).

Malgrés quelques bonnes idées le jeu rebute par le manque de maitrise de son deck et sa difficulté.

À jouer avec la bande son des films bien entendu.

RATING: 6.5
A personal favorite theme with some good story telling ability with a good amount of suspense; true to the nature of the movie. Outside of this however I feel the game falls a little flat. I feel characters are obviously pigeonholed to build a certain type of deck so there is a sense of false choice there. Unfortunately I feel this game also falls victim to the fact that the best/most efficient actions are very obvious. This leads to an overall feeling that you're essentially flipping over a bunch of cards, playing the most obvious best card/combo and hope you don't come up empty when a tough encounter appears. That's not to say there is no choice at all but I feel the fate of the shuffle weighs very heavy in this game. Fun to play out a scenario in a high suspense story telling manner but I wouldn't mistake this for a strategy/tactical game with hard decisions.

RATING: 9
Played about 10 solo games and a single 2 player game (with hidden agenda and alien player rules). Playing through all the movie scenarios first.

So far, this has been an excellent game. Really captures the mood of the movies. I don't normally enjoy solo games but this has kept my attention for a few days now. I think it will be a lot of fun when the game group meets. Sometimes the sequence of card flips and events really gives on the feel of being 'in the story', which is a pretty cool accomplishment for a card game.

Hard to say for sure, but the Alien (film 1) scenario seems really challenging to beat (that's good...took about 6 plays to win). Aliens (2) seems a bit too easy (played twice, won twice). Aliens3 was pretty easy the first and only time I played. Have not finished an Alien Resurrection based game yet.

If the game gets too easy with multi-players with the coordinate ability, it's easy enough to tweak the game according to the rule suggestions or even using the spare blank cards (i.e. as Barracks filler that takes up space in the HQ for a turn (or more)).

Giving it only a 9 because I've only played less than a week and the box didn't come filled with money or chocolate.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Has a much stronger thematic feel than Marvel Legendary at the expense of having less scenarios. However, like Marvel Legendary has a bunch of effects that are pretty luck based (e.g. the effects that make you lose a random 1+ cost in your hand). In addition while there doesseem to be less really swingy luck based cards as Marvel Legendary (Feast, Loki's Father of Lies card, etc.) I really dislike the lack of ability to mill cards in the game.

The stronger thematic feel comes from 1: the mastermind not just sitting there the whole game for the most part not doing anything 2. each hero having a slightly different starting deck 3. scenarios that change more as the game is played (3 objectives per scenario with the events/hazards changing depending on which objective you're on) 4. monsters attacking you when they "escape". This is contrary to Marvel Legendary, where depending on the scheme there is often a significant population of villains that has no penalty when escaping. The "Coordinate" key word also makes the game more of a co-op instead of half multiplayer solitaire. Unfortunately this comes at the price of only have 4 scenarios in the game (albeit with several modules you can add on e.g. traitors). If I owned this game it would be fun creating my own scenarios but alas, the luck swings I mentioned in the previous paragraph makes this game not good enough to buy for me.

I don't understand why everyone thinks this game is so hard, unless you're playing with the traitor. Yes I was playing it as 2 players which meant my deck was a lot less diluted, yes I have a lot of deck building experience, and yes we technically probably should have lost because we accidentally scanned a room with a hazard before killing an alien, but we really didn't utilize the -2 health things in the second wave of the second scenario well, and we played it out, and if we had resolved things in the opposite order would have won with things quite under control. We also had 3 hive cards played to start with and used only 2-1-0 instead of 2-2-2 of the weak aliens.

RATING: 8
Great fusion of mechanics and theme.  It feels like you are playing the movies, including the same level of suspense and intensity.  This has lots of life in it, as you can replay each scenario without knowing the flow or outcome.  The mixing of objectives/location adds a lot of possibilities.  Semi-compatible with other Legendary titles, but it can be done with online research and some creativity.  Solo play is challenging and enjoyable.  Difficulty can be increased or decreased.  Plus you can add a traitor element.  Lots of variety in the base game, perhaps more than Legendary Marvel.  It has the same limitations as Legendary Marvel: set-up/teardown takes a few minutes, 3-player game is the sweet spot, & rules can be a bit daunting to new players.  Overall, if you like deck-builders and love the Alien franchise, you will love this game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Marvel Legendary was a complete dud for me for several reasons, but mainly due to it being too easy and I wasn't a fan of the semi-coop nature of the game.  

Legendary Encounters surpasses it in many ways.  It is more difficult, but you can also adjust the difficulty by changing how many drones you add to the hive deck.  It's a pure coop and adds in Coordinate cards to help your teammates.  There is added tension since you need to scan locations to see what kind of aliens will pop out at you, but you're using up your attack power to do it.  You have to balance when to attack and when to scan more locations.  There are objectives to work towards - such as trapping a particular alien in a specific location to defeat them or setting up sentry guns.  

Maybe my rating will drop with more plays (currently at 10+), but it is a highly addictive game for me right now.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
An excellent game that replicates the heart pounding tension of the Alien franchise very well.  To me, it also has a bit of a legacy game aspect since certain cards that come up may have certain permanent affects for the rest of the game and there's definitely a campaign feel to the game with the different objective, but without any replayability concerns. Speaking of replayability, no concerns here.  You can mix and match objectives, locations, and character decks across the 4 movies completely, plus there are advanced rules with hidden agendas and players who can actually become the alien!  If you are a fan of the Alien franchise or co-op games in general, this is a must-own.

RATING: 3
Thematically wonderful, mechanically it's deeply flawed.

It's more than just the multiple random elements potentially magnifying each other (for the players or against), but also things like the Alien players removing cards from players hands - effectively removing their ability to actually play the game or offer any counter play.

The first game we played, we should not have won, we were deep in the hole, and got a string of luck that enabled the win.

The second game we played, the trader outed immediately, nabbed a face hugger (via luck), and because an Alien before anything could be done by another player.  They then proceeded to get a second player infected, again without counter play ability.  In short order the two were aliens, and got a third infected.  All the while removing cards from the remaining players hands - resulting in the Aliens having all the actions/turns and the humans having none.  It was runaway with no counterplay - which is what you get when the players removing or destroy cards from player hands rather than inserting cards or manipulating the environment (poor design).  

Absolute shame, the theme is wonderful. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.8
I'm looking for any excuse to enjoy the Alien IP, so this game makes me happy. This is my kind of deck builder.

RATING: 9
I haven't felt this wrapped up in a co-op game since the first time I played [gameid=823]. This was the highlight of BGG.CON 2014 for me. The thematic quality is top-notch. 

It takes the Legendary system, makes it completely cooperative and then adds a new keyword [b]Coordinate[/b] to help include all players each turn.

Especially cool is that players can become Aliens (then using a second deck) or traitors. The game can be quite difficult at times. Unlike [gameid=129437] you can't just fight Villains (Hive here) when they pop out. They rooms they're in first need to be Scanned (using Attack power). So the Aliens begin adding up quite quickly. In fact I would say they're probably impossible without the new Coordinate mechanism. 

Only issue with this game so far is the player elimination. In a multi-player game it's possible for someone to get knocked out fairly early. Here Wounds take away your hit points... if they're not healed, and some cannot be, you die.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
The good - Great game, great mechanics. The artwork is almost perfect with the only proviso being it is in comic book form. What would have made it absolutely 100% perfect? Resurrecting Giger from the grave and having him do the cards. Either that or a more black and white Sin City approach. The cards fit in the box, even sleeved. Thankfully no vacuum molded divider that breaks in a week and wont fit the cards if sleeved. Game mat is great and fits in the box. 

The bad - All of this is real nitpicking. The decks come shrink wrapped in about ten packs and none of them are collated. This means initial sleeving and set up literally goes on for hours. I timed myself and it took over four hours to separate, sleeve and collate all the cards into their appropriate decks. The worst is the fact that the graphic design is horrendous (graphic design is different from artwork). For example - Event and Hazard cards go with specific decks. How do you know which deck? Get out a microscope and look for the teeny tiny type at the bottom of the card which indicates the deck it goes with. I was half way through setup before I saw this on the Event cards so make sure you take a good look for the tiny type at the bottom. The only other thing I would change is the card backs. Graphic design that was a little more Alien oriented would have been really nice here. It is totally weird to me that with all the time spent on great artwork for the mat and the cards it seems like the card backs were an afterthought. This could be solved through using sleeves with a cool back but it really seems anyone looking at the game with cards on the mat should have spoken up and said "you know, super hero blue with that logo really doesn't fit with all this other great stuff" 

Great game, my complaints really are just nitpicking, I would highly recommend getting this one.

RATING: 7
Legendary: Alien covers all 4 Alien movies and somehow manages to convey both the theme and feel of each of those movies individually which I think is an amazing feat in itself, let alone from a card game!

It is very easy to understand and play, and because its totally coop has quite a light and breezy feel to it despite the depressive tone of the Alien movies.

There's so many things I like about how the game works and its so damn clever I honestly can't level much criticism against it!

One major point is that the number of players taking part drastically adjusts the difficulty level- 4 players makes the game so much harder then with 3 players you wouldn't believe the difference.

I heard there's also a Predator version coming soon. If its anything like this it will be worth having a go at.

RATING: 6
[B]TTS Play:[/B] Played the crap out of this one...  Initial movie set up (Alien) played alright.  There was tension, but also some awkward downtime while cycling cards.  May need to skip drones, as the complexity was a bit questionable.  Despite all that, it was enjoyable and definitely worth playing to go through the four movies. The final objective brought a world of hurt and my deck was sorely lacking (need to buy more purchase power during the early game).  The difficulty ramp redeems the game somewhat, but reveals its lack of solo play balance as many of the mechanics require multiple players.  Perhaps play with two hands would be interesting - or a major headache...  Fifth play was very different - totally schooled the alien beeaches. I did get to 10/11 strikes, but was able to heal once...  Enjoyed this one...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
This game shares the mechanisms with other Legendary games and it's partially compatible with them. I have not tried that.

It's a cooperative card game that tries to recreate the 4 Alien movies. We actually played the first Alien movie and it didn't seem anything like it. The second one is more like it, but even if the theme is there, it's not the theme feast some people claim.

The cooperative mechanics feel a bit artificial, but they work very well, mechanics wise.

Players have some roles that create differences and asymmetry between them. It becomes a bit dilluted as the deck grows, but it's ok.

Things I'm not a fan of:
-> Immense setup time (and also to sort out the cards after finishing).
-> Player elimination: can occur quite soon in the game. People will say it's not likely, but it's happened to me more than once.
-> Not a lot of options each turn, you don't have a lot of choices: you cards choose for you.
-> Basically you do the same from the first turn to the last one. You just have more powerful cards and enemies.
-> The deckbuilding aspect is not interesting. Not a lot of diversity, the combos are obvious and they force you to embark on a set path, and no real possibilities to prune your deck. At the end game it becomes huge and the luck of the draw becomes very important.

The thing I like the least is that I got the impression that the adventure was laid up for me to play it, we first have the same level 1 resurce cards and we face the same level 1 enemies, then we continue with the same level 2 resources and enemies, etc. It all seems very artificial to me, it is like a linear role playing adventure. I already played the first adventure and I think that playing it again will be no different. And the game contains too many cards and is way too expensive for such a limited replayability.

The components are not great. The cardstock is average at most, the illustrations/graphic are just OK (they could have been much better considering all the Alien stuff there's already around). The playmat though is excelent!

First impression [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/geeklist/184429/item/3906811#item3906811]here[/url].

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Enjoyable for what it is, but I find it less 'thematic' (although I don't really like this word, or the word 'theme', since it suggests a sort of superficial version of 'subject matter', which is what I prefer to speak of) than everyone else seems to. Characters from the films appear on the cards, but you don't actually play as those characters. You play as a generic medic, mercenary, or what have you. Also, it's a little odd that your character can usually survive several close combat strikes from the aliens, whereas in the films getting that close was invariably deadly for humans. The net result of all this is what could be called 'thematic dissonance', a feeling that the Alien subject matter has been dealt with in a way that is 'imaginatively confused', for want of a better term.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Some different monster processing rules, but your turns are much the same experience as the original game. Draw your cards, acquire as many heroes as you can, kill as many monsters as you can. Get powers that feed off each other. It maintains the long setup and long putaway which was a major impediment in the original. It adds a more realistic and relevant (to my generation) theme, which is upside. The monster mechanics are better, and I like how there's increased pressure to kill stuff because random Hit Points are added directly to your hero for each one you don't kill off (rather than adding wounds to your deck). You'd think that not adding wounds to the deck would allow deck management to be easier, but my initial games here never really had enough turns to get my deck tuned enough to get synergies going. And of course getting synergistic turns is where the fun is in deck-builders, so this was a downer compared to the original. If you're keen, choose the one with the more attractive theme to you, otherwise it doesn't add much to the genre.
