RATING: 8
"Compared to Legendary Marvel, I like that it is pure co-op. But it has player elimination (or betrayal), and isn't as good solo as the Golden solo variant for Marvel. The narrative arc is great, and the theme comes through, but you still feel like a manager more than a single character. Setup is non-trivial, but perhaps not as bad as some say."

What I like:
- Pure co-op (if you ignore the alien players and traitors)
- Very thematic
- Smooth engine similar to Legendary Marvel and Ascension
- Player mat works quite well (although it's a bit too long to fit crosswise on our table)
- Coordinate keyword is excellent

What I don't like:
- [b]Mini-deck identifiers should have been larger!!![/b]
- Box is an awkward size
- The game can feel like a brutal beat-down
- I'm not familiar with the Alien movies, and would prefer a less bloody theme
- Solo play loses the Coordinate keyword, so probably not as good as the Legendary Marvel "Golden" variant

I would put the weight around 2.8, just slightly above BGG voters.

RATING: 8.5
10+ plays - A great team game. A lot of fun and if you know the movies, it's even better. The mat is what really makes the game imo. The card organisation is a little tricky the first time, but I can pack this game up and down eerily fast now - label your dividers!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Legendary Encounters is a cooperative deckbuilding game.  Monsters and other threats (as well as mission objectives) come out in a queue, and as they reach the active area, you have to deal with them or take wounds every round.  You can buy cards from a replenishing pool, and the cards have icons that make them work well in combination (though the effect of this seemed limited to me).  Some cards can be loaned to other players in an attempt to simulate cooperation.  This game clearly isn't aimed at me, as I'm a fan of neither cooperative games nor the Alien franchise. That said, I guess it did the things you'd want a deckbuilding coop to do. But I'm not the best judge here.

(1 play)

RATING: 9.5
This game is a must-have for any fan of the Alien franchise. Like other deck building games, Alien comes with a substantial amount of cards with some really great artwork. Additionally, players also get a very large custom mat, also with lots of great artwork. Plays up to 5 people and allows users to play through the various movies (Alien, Aliens, Alien 3, and Alien Resurrection). Dying isn't the end of this game either. Players who receive a facehugger and the sometimes inevitable chestburster can come back as the dreaded Xenomorph to attack the other survivors. Highly recommended.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I've you've played Legendary Marvel, there's a lot you'll recognise about this game. Essentially, this game is a deck builder where players buy new cards from a belt of cards, hoping to accumulate combos for the future, which will be used to defeat the belt of enemy cards. Each scenario has special rules for victory, which in this case is themed for the various Alien movies.

The art is a little weak to what I'm used to from reading Dark Horse Alien comic books from the 80s and 90s, but it's reasonably standard for a game in the Legendary series. Mechanically, I enjoy that this game is fully co-op as opposed to the strange system in the main Legendary games line where you are working together but also fighting for the most points. To that end, there's an awesome little mechanic here that allows you to assist another player during their turn by playing your assist card and then redrawing, helping you to cycle around to your better cards. Another fantastic element is that players have a character card which however much health, and wounds just stack up at the side of your board, rather than crapping up your card draws.

I liked Marvel Legendary, but I got annoyed by the semi-co-op nature, plus the unwieldiness of all the expansions, plus the focus on 90s characters and art really got to me. Legendary Alien brings along none of that baggage and doubles down on the things I liked about the game.

:star: Art, Iconography and components functional
:star: Clever or interesting mechanisms
:star: Reasonably low downtime between turns with mildly AP players
:star: Multiple plays stay interesting
:star: Low or mitigatable luck elements
:star::star::star::nostar::nostar: Raw enjoyment
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
Like new, played once.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
A fun and pretty thematic deck building game. I definitely like it better than Marvel Legendary, mostly because of the Coordinate cards that add in more to think about during other people's turns and give the game more of a truly cooperative feel.
There are some issues that keep it from being great, though. The theming is a bit weird in that it's unclear what the player is, thematically. You aren't one of the characters, because you are buying cards with multiple characters on them. You aren't some external agent. It's not a huge deal, but it keeps the theme from really feeling real. Also, while there are more meaningful decisions than in Marvel Legendary, there is a lot of randomness in the game, and at higher player counts it can feel very hard to improve your situation by playing well. There just aren't that many decisions to make during each turn.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
As a semi-cooperative alien deckbuilder, I really expected this to be bloated, confusing, and imbalanced. After one play, I was very happy to find that it was none of these things. It was relatively easy to understand the options I had on my turn, and I felt that the decisions were usually non-obvious. I have never seen any of the Alien movies and I do not typically enjoy alien themes in games, but I did have fun playing this game.

I also want to give props to the coordinate mechanic. I consider this mechanic an absolute triumph of design, and I wouldn't be surprised to see future games steal it. The choice between helping yourself or a potentially traitorous ally is phenomenally engaging. We've seen this explored in games such as Battlestar Galactica before, but Legendary's clean implementation is the best yet, and  the coordinate cards are very important to the group's success, giving the game great tension.

There are other good things to talk about. The damage system provides a sense of danger while being very easy to understand. The rules are MOSTLY clear, as far as game rules go. A few minor negatives: setup/teardown is annoying, the order the enemies come out from the deck has a huge effect on ability to win, and the complexity is just a bit too high to play with non-gamers who love the movies, but without all those elements, the game wouldn't be as engaging, so honestly there is nothing ti complain about here. 

Put it all together, and it's almost impossible to believe that this thing comes from Upper Deck of all companies. Consider this their announcement that they are joining the big leagues.

RATING: 8
17-06-2015. Sold after 7 plays. I felt I got enough of the game. I like it, but it's not a game that feels fresh and interesting anymore. I still like it and would play again.

13-06-2015. Rated after 5 plays. Alien Encounter is the evolution of a game system I previously played and did not really enjoyed but felt was ok. Aliens changes the system.
You start the game by building a Hive deck and the Barracks, which based on the movie you want to play or random if you want to do that.

Each turn, you move a card from the Hive deck, a deck filled with Aliens, Hazards and events, facedown into the Complex. If there is no empty slot, the previous cards slide down towards the Airlock or combat zone if the Complex is fully filled. 

In  your action phase, you buy new cards and play cards for damage. There is also a cool mechanism with special abilities you can trigger by playing them if the types of previous cards align. Another cool twist is that you can coordinate with other players, allowing them to play an exact copy of the card you have and you replacing it with a new card. Interesting.

Then, if there are enemies in the combat zone they attack. Damage is random, but can consist of facehuggers that can mutate into chestbursters that can kill you in a later turn.

This game is very cool. I am no big fan of Aliens OR of Legendary, but this game has warmed me up to the system. It's good, I enjoy it and I think it's excellent.

RATING: 10
Definitely a good game.
Reminiscent of earlier deck builders like Thunderstone, this masterpiece is a lot more polished than its predecessors.
The theme and mechanics are integrated together seamlessly, granting a truly captivating game experience.

 - Fast set up (once the initial organization of the contents is complete). 
 - Interesting and effective decisions to be made throughout all phases of the game.
 - Strong narrative, creating your own unique story.
 - Build up of tension through the session as encounters grow tougher and you hope your previous decisions will give you the might to defeat them. 
 - The ability to plan for and mitigate the random confrontations and events that get thrown at you.
 - Medium play time that allows multiple games in a session.

I expect to exhaust the core game sometime in 2018, so really looking forward to getting the expansion to fill my time for the following four years.
Although, I probably will be playing it again from the start, by then! 

Finally doing the whole Mix 'n' Match thing has revitalised this game for me.
Although I think of myself as a purest and disliked the idea of deviating from the movie scripts, the change in card interactions gives you new challenges and dynamics.
The games are just as enjoyable and still provide the interactions and decisions to experience an legendary saga.

RATING: 8
If you are familiar with Marvel Legendary, this is a re-skin of the game in the Ridley Scott Alien universe with a few rules variations.

The main heft of the game is the same.  There is a deck of "heroes" (in this case characters from the four Alien movies) that you draft into your personal deck.  Each round you play your hand of cards to generate attack and buy power to buy more heroes or attack the bad guys which enter a line of locations from another deck.  The heroes all display the same symbols from Marvel Legendary that fuel the powers of other heroes the same way.

So what is different?  First all the heroes take on a specific identity.  These identities set a player's health, armor (only used in an advanced play mode), and give each player a special card to start.  Also, enemies enter the board face down and need to be scanned with attack power based on the location they are in before you can attack them.  The game also is won or lost based on 3 objectives and the enemy deck has many different cards in it from aliens you fight to obstacles related to the objective to Facehuggers.  That's another addition, if a player gets a Facehugger they have 2 turns to defeat it (and sometimes you get it at the end of a turn after you've already used all your cards so you really only have one, this happened to me in my first game) or they add a Chestburster card to their deck.  When the Chestburster card is drawn the player dies and becomes an alien player playing against the other players.

You can also play that the Chestburster card just kills the player instead of transforming him.  We played that it turned that player into an alien because that's more fun, especially for the player who would have to just sit out otherwise.  However this presents a very Shadows Over Camelot-esque problem.  I often felt Marvel Legendary was a bit too easy out-of-box.  This game seems to address that a bit and feels a bit more challenging even with everyone playing cooperatively.  The alien players really skew this though.  They get to play 6 cards a turn, all of which really ruin the other players days.  It was incredibly difficult, bordering on impossible for players to make any progress once an alien player is in the game having to fight against the game itself and another, extremely powerful, disruptive force.

All in all, the changes from Marvel Legendary all seem for the better.  I like the atmosphere it creates and the game feels a lot more focused in the experience it is trying to present to the players.  I will say the theme is one that I'm less interested in/familiar with than Marvel super-heroes.  I've seen 3 of the 4 Alien movies but they never really grabbed me so I care a lot less and even barely know any of the characters I draft into my deck in this game.  That does dock it some in my eyes but it is still a great game experience.

It may be worth mentioning that this game can be combined with some parts of the Marvel Legendary game and vice versa but the rules for that are a little hokey, it's probably best just to keep them separate.  But the options is there if you just really want Ripley and Spider-Man to team up against Dormammu and a Xenomorph.

RATING: 5.5
Clever co-op deckbuilding game descended from Ascension, most notable for its somewhat successful attempts at thematic integration. The structure of the game is relatively straightforward: on a player's turn they draw an enemy card, which joins the queue advancing towards them along the station track. Enemies turn face up either when they reach the end ("combat zone") or when a player ability scans one. Some cards are instant events etc. or otherwise have abilities when revealed, so scanning is not without risk. Cards remaining in the combat zone after a player's turn hurt them, requiring damage cards to be drawn from the strike deck.

The pile of cards players can buy from is assembled by combining smaller decks of cards representing characters from the film; the enemy deck is built from three smaller decks representing key plot points. In its most thematic format, players can roughly follow the plot of the first four Alien films, but of course the sub-decks can be mixed and matched for alternate-universe variety.

The theme does work relatively well. The enemy deck structure ensures that the difficulty ramps up quickly, and early tension (and a nice thematic twist) comes from the facehugger cards, which can appear suddenly and must be dealt with immediately; if they stay too long, the affected player puts a chestburster in their deck, which instantly kills them when drawn. (A variant allows a player thus afflicted to continue on as an enemy alien.)

As a game it is only light or medium weight and randomness plays a significant role. Damage from the strike deck ranges from 0-5, which does add tension to the draw but also makes survival a total crapshoot. Significant variation (Ascension style) in the character deck likewise makes achieving card synergies potentially challenging; some cards are unique and will very likely never turn up in any given game. To smooth out this randomness the design leans heavily on the ability of players to lend certain cards out in other players' turns, but no allowance is made for the number of players available to do so (for obvious reasons fewer in a 2p than a 5p game). 

Ultimately it's thematic chrome on an uninteresting engine and players' enjoyment is contingent on their enjoyment of making a story out of random events. I would suggest a roleplaying game instead.

One minor annoyance is the hugely painful setup and teardown, which is compounded by failure to spring for different backs for different types of card. This is not a game you want to play 600-card pickup with.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Thunderstone in space. Except you don't even have to make a decision whether to go to the village (shopping) or the dungeon (fighting) as you automatically do both. And there is no light parameter, but simply an increasing 'scan' cost to simulate a growing row of monsters to fight. Traps are simulated by events and hazards, treasures are the characters you find. So basically, it is a simplified version of Thunderstone.

Now, it does some clever things on its own, like adding attributes (like Vigilante) to your cards so you can manage your tableau even better. Also it introduces a 'Coordinate' mechanism which basically bogs down to 'always play it' as you get a replacement draw (hence every decent deckbuilder knows this will speed up your deck as well, so it is an automatic thing to do) and just pick someone you think can use it. Also, the Facehugger mechanism is a nice touch. These suddenly pop up into your face and you have to kill them immediately or else face inescapable death in the near future.

Luckily, that will almost never happen, as the biggest drawback of the game is that sadly, it is too easy. Monsters don't go into your deck, so you can tune your deck way better as in Thunderstone. The result of that is that if you follow the default route of deckbuilding (start culling as soon as possible, focus on cards that increase your spending power early on and just over half the game start focusing on the 'battle' cards) , by objective 2 you 'control' the game, meaning you've cleared out the Complex and just finish off whatever poor bastard will show up next as soon as there is a new one. As there is no way to 'speed up' the game, this becomes a boring, repetitive affair as you wait for the final wrench that might spice things up, but have to go through the repetitive motion of draw, buy cards (or pass on that), finish up, redraw. And as there is no way to 'cycle' the HQ (the shop), you are not even being rewarded for being in control. Blegh.

Finally, I feel the setup for the players is simply not diversified enough. You have no special abilities of your own, just one card in your starting deck of 14 will differ. Big whoop. In Sentinels of the Multiverse, another coop card game going up against the bad guys, you get a whole deck of different cards, PLUS a unique power to take with you. Here you're basically the next dude, save that one card.

Theme wise, it is done very nice. Artwork is done well and with a playmat the game absolutely looks gorgeous. But this is not enough to salvage my gripes of Alien: Legendary Encounters. As far as the mechanics go, I like Star Realms for its simplicity and quick playing time. Thunderstone for the meater 'build your deck' experience, and Sentinels of the Multiverse better as a cooperative game because of the asymmetric abilities this game lacks. 

This game? For trade.

RATING: 6
A surprisingly good deck building coop game.

Pros: Super fast gameplay for an otherwise quite rewarding game combined with a fairly fast setup and increased difficulty creates a "let's go for another one" spirit. Dark and very armospheric - the theme works miracles. Cooperation is essential and very well supported, players can't play by themselves. Very fun and agonising gameplay. Serious decisions that are not obvious initially. A very simple game system that is easy to learn and get into that is however stretched to its total strategic limits and as a result allows for great variability and strategy. Excellent flow of play and pacing. Extra modes (traitor and may turn into allien modes) are welcome.

Cons: It's still a very basic system, mechanics wise. Why the rule "When a player is killed the others have one last round to finish the mission" is optional in coop mode is beyond me. Player elimination was a serious issue in our games until we added it.

Overall, it's a very fast and enjoyable, if fairly simple, cooperative game.

RATING: 9.5
This one combines my favourite film franchises with one of my favourite mechanics, deck-building. While I really liked Marvel Legendary, it had some problems and I didn't like the theme, which is strange since I really love Marvel comics. When Alien was announce I had my reservations but those quickly went away when I tried the game. It feels so thematic. Everything from the Chestburster in your deck to the (optional) hidden traitor and Alien player is just right. We've played this game so much and it still manages to beat us, which is really good for a coop game. 

Despite some of the games issues - flimsy cards, bad/inconsistent art and a long setup/tear-down time - I still love it and even frequently play it solo. In fact, it's probably my most-played solo game - though, to be fair, I actually don't play a lot of solo games. 

When played at my game group, we frequently play with both the hidden traitor AND Alien player modules and it's a hoot. We always end up quoting the film too, which, for me, just makes it even better. Definitely one of my favourite coop games out there.

Also own expansion.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
I was really excited to play this game, as cooperative games are my favorite kind, and this title had a lot of buzz regarding its quality. And I'm pleased to say it lived up to the hype. [thing=146652][/thing] is a good game, with some neat mechanics - the way the enemies and events run by the locations hidden is neat and tense, as we can see the threats advancing, without knowing what they are, unless we scan the place, which can, in turn, lead to even more nastiness. The game play is mostly the same as in Legendary - deckbuilding with two "currencies" - attack (to kill the aliens) and influence (to acquire new cards). Cards to purchase come all from the same deck, and a new one is revealed after one in the track is taken. 

[thing=146652][/thing] is based in scenarios, mostly similar to the movies - in the first scenario, Nostromo, for instance, the final goal is to kill the Perfect Organism. Once the enemies reach the combat zone, they will start to attack the players, making them, on their turns, to draw from the strike deck, which will, most of the time, cause injury to the characters - if the damage reaches the total HP of characters, he/she will be killed, and out of the play. There is another possibility: if a Facehugger isn't killed while it is in the play area, a Chest Buster will enter the character deck, and if it is drawn by the player, the character will be killed, but not out the game - he/she will start to play for the enemy!

The decisions are all that hard to be made - is mostly which card to buy (usually vying for combos, using cards of the same icon, like in regular Legendary), which enemy to attack and/or where to scan. Scan is done blindly - there is no way to know what will appear (and, well, how could be otherwise, right?). Which alien to attack is often given, either because there will be only one, or because if you have a lot of attack, you will normally attack the alien that is tougher to beat - this is only slightly changed when there is a Facehugger showing, as, as mentioned, these could became nastier than most.

There is plenty of luck of the draw: in the players deck, in the draw deck and in the enemy deck - in this last one the goal cards are shuffled, much in the way it happens in [thing=30549][/thing], as the cards are divided and the goal cards are shuffled in the parts, so players know that X card is among the, say, first 10, and the Y card among the 11 and 20, and so on. The luck of the draw can be a little reduced by the addition of Coordinate cards - these can be played by other players during someone else's turn in order to double the effect of a card used - this, besides talking about the the best way to proceed (which place to scan, who to heal, and so on), is the cooperation in the game.

As one could expect, deck builders aren't really the best mechanic to create a cooperative game, as the very nature of a person building her own deck is mostly a solitaire business. The Coordinate card is mainly all the interaction allowed by the game. One player can't, say, put his character in front of other to protect it from damage, nor they can share ammo, or split to cover more ground (ok, this part is good that can't happen). Maybe this can occur in later scenarios, but I'm not holding my breath. Still, the Coordinate is key to win and, considering several cards have this key-word (including the Sergeant card, that is a basic card, always present), Coordinate can happen often, so there is definitely a sense of cooperation between players, even if not as much as some other games.

The cards are a little on the flimsy side, but the game mat is awesome - is made of rubbery canvas (maybe "canvas" isn't the proper word, but I can't think of another to fit), and it feels great (and it doesn't have "memory" - i.e.: it doesn't curve the tips).

The bad part of [thing=146652][/thing] is the player elimination, a mechanic that, while thematic (and is necessary to properly give a sense of dread), can lead to someone leaving early (as there are some high damage cards in the strike deck, dealing 4, even 5 damage at once) and just watching the game go on - however, a play last around 45 minutes, so isn't going to be all that bad, but is worth mentioning - it would be good if the rules allowed for a "killed" character to be actually just badly hurt, so, instead of drawing a full hand of cards, the player would draw, say, 3 cards - enough to still do some things, and be in the game, but still so weak as to be, sometimes, carried by the others(could be really thematic, as a bleeding character is taken foward by her teammates; so the strike cards would be given to someone else - enhancing the cooperative feel of cooperation).

Overall, [thing=146652][/thing] is a good cooperative game, dynamic and tense, that doesn't go "easy" on players, even in the first scenario. The rules and flow are easy to understand, specially if the players already know [thing=129437][/thing]. There is truly a feel of the movies in the game - the unknown approach of aliens, and then you see the blip in the scan, but you don't know if you will be able to deal with everything, even with help, as the aliens are some tough nut to crack, and the damage is pilling on.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
A clever, cooperative deck-building game tailor made for fans of the Aliens films that captures the desperation of battling. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
"...we just got our asses kicked, pal!"

Brutally difficult. Surprisingly thematic. Much more player interaction that I'd expected with two separate traitor mechanics. Did I mention brutally difficult?

Component quality is excellent, the artwork captures the films brilliantly while avoiding cheap cast shots and film stills which can look tacky. The rulebook is clear and well presented.

The only real downside is the sorting and labelling dividers: took the best part of an evening and even now the set up/ pack up is still relatively long. The neutral character cards which make up your starting deck, as well as the 'drone' card, feel a little incongruous in terms of simulating the first two films.

That said, gameplay works superbly and will be familiar to anyone who has played other deckbuilders. The mechanics did a great job of capturing the escalating tension and bursts of frantic action which characterise the films. The objective, hazard and event cards add masses of thematic flavour. We got lots of fun out of the constant references to movie lines which the advanced HQ cards make.

This is an absolute beast of a deckbuilder for anyone who enjoys sci-fi /horror. Pretty essential for fans of the films.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
We've only tried the first two movie scenarios, but at the moment this is my favorite Legendary product.  I truly enjoy Marvel Legendary and its endless expansions, so this is a genuine surprise.

Our last game (Aliens scenario) was particularly amazing, to the point where I considered a rating of 9 rather than 'only' an 8.  Both other players had been killed, and I was left to survive on my own for 10+ turns.  But my deck was sufficiently well tuned with vicious attacks and Vigilant armor that I eventually managed to send Mother to the acidic alien afterlife.

Lots of Pros: The stacked Hive deck creates a nice progression through the movie storyline(s), the gameplay integrates neat thematic elements (e.g., sentry guns and ventilation shafts), each character has a special starting card, the Coordination mechanic is great, and four completely independent scenarios provide good value for the money.

A few cons: The game is supposedly impossible to win with 4-5 players, but we've heeded the community warnings and only played with 2-3.  The Alien scenario (#1) occasionally results in early player death (my insides are on the outside! that's bad!), which is frustrating for the player who gets knocked out in 10-15 minutes - particularly since it can be almost unavoidable.  Though we ignore the advanced 'transform into alien' rules, as the game is hard enough without a former ally becoming an active opponent.

Anyway, I'm extremely glad that I traded a grail game for this and Legendary Predator.  If Predator is as good as this one, the trade will go down in history as my best swap ever.

Alien also has me looking forward to the Legendary versions of Firefly and Big Trouble in Little China, which is unexpected (and hurtful, money-wise).

RATING: 9
What I like of this game:
- I like Alien movies very much and this game catches the spirit very well.
- It's very very very easy to learn.
- It's very well balanced and you can adjust the difficulty to play it harder or easier.

What I don't like of this game:
- Count with 2 or 3 hours to sort all cards after unboxing. The box is a mess.
- Hundreds of cards and the box is terrible, I don't know how to store the cards, and you probably will have to make a custom box, or custom dividers to have the game organized.
- I don't understand what happens with the art, some cards are amazing and the characters are very well represented. But other cards are just...well I will try to be polite and just say awful.

Conclusion: The bad things are related to game "hardware" and the theme and mechanics are so good that this makes me have a great experience, so I give it a 9.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I've never played any of the other Legendary games.  But, as a HUGE fan of the Alien series, this game delivers.  I won't necessarily say it would be for everyone.  And some of the added optional gameplay elements don't work nearly as well as one would hope (the *turn into an alien when you die* thing never really happens, and the *hidden traitor* addition is BROKEN.  I'll have to look up an errata for how to play with the traitor...  it should work, but somehow doesn't....  hard to explain).  But as a co-op game goes, if you like the theme, you will enjoy this game.  I guess my biggest complaint is that, while I'm sure there are cool card interactions if you combine LE with some of the other Legendary games, by itself, some of the scenarios (ie, each movie) feel like they really only work internally.  When you mix them together, you often end up with cards that REQUIRE some interaction (such as the *coordinate* mechanic) that you just didn't accommodate for when you selected your character decks.  
But, it's not a deal breaker: if you're an Alien fan, you will really enjoy playing through the movie beats - even the ones you aren't a fan of.  The objectives are fun, and the theme is really there.
Word of caution though:  like everyone else who has ever reviewed this game sais, you CAN'T play this straight out of the box.  you NEED to set aside an hour to sort through the poorly organized cards.  It's not complicated, but it is akin to buying a piece of IKEA furniture and trying to piece it all together.  Without the instructions.  Blindfolded.    
Well, maybe not that bad.  But until you sort through, learn and organize the cards, it will feel like someone threw all the cards on the ground and told you to play 52-pick up.  with ~600 cards....
Ya.... Not cool.  Not cool.  Manufactures and designers take note:  this is how to potentially alienate (no pun intended) people from what is actually a good game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Most enjoyable game I have played in a long time.  Richly thematic with constant tension due to the steady flow of unseen cards into the Complex.  A win really feels like an accomplishment, and a loss is not at all disheartening (dying to the Aliens feels appropriately thematic as well). 

There may not be much strategic depth to this game.  I think the most important decisions relate to recruiting strategy; ensuring the maximum opportunities for important combos and just as importantly, knowing when to stop recruiting so as to keep your deck as efficient as possible.  

However, for me this game is much more experiential than tactical, and on that level it hits a grand slam (in the bottom of the ninth, world series game seven no less)! 

Thanks!
